RTL8761BU Libre Firmware — Work in Progress
============================================
Goal: free/libre replacement for rtl8761bu_fw.bin for linux-libre / UB500 dongle.
Based on Xeno Kovah's RE research (Hardwear.io NL 2025).
Primary analysis tool: Ghidra headless via wairz MCP.
Primary binary: 2026-04-25_rtl8761buv_USB_fw-and-ROM.bin.gzf


PHASE 1 — UNDERSTAND THE PATCH MECHANISM
-----------------------------------------
[DONE] Set up Ghidra headless analysis via wairz MCP
[DONE] Extract Kovah's function annotations → analysis/kovah_function_list.md
[DONE] Analyze master patch installer FUN_80103780
         → analysis/reverse_engineering_patch_installer.md
         → 50+ function pointers installed, 6 sub-installers called, full phase map
[DONE] Analyze LMP VSC hook FUN_8010bba4 (bos_base+0xd8)
         → analysis/reverse_engineering_lmp_vsc_hook.md
[DONE] Analyze VSC opcode dispatcher
         → analysis/reverse_engineering_vsc_dispatcher.md
[DONE] Analyze connection record subsystem struct layout
         → analysis/reverse_engineering_conn_record_subsystem.md
[DONE] Analyze ROM FUN_8004f824 (slot-budget validator + hw hook dispatcher)
         → analysis/reverse_engineering_hardware_layer.md
         → Hook at 0x801212e4 is the ONLY path to actual baseband register writes


PHASE 2 — MAP ALL INSTALLED HOOKS (IN PROGRESS)
-------------------------------------------------
[DONE]  Identify the function installed at RAM hook slot 0x801212e4 (2026-06-08)
          RESOLVED: NOT installed by the patch. Installed by ROM FUN_80025b68
          at SCO/eSCO connection setup time. That ROM function writes runtime-
          generated MIPS16e code (from ROM codec tables PTR_DAT_80025ca8/cac)
          into conn_record._x58+0x13e and sets +0xe4 → +0x13e as the hook ptr.
          Full GZF scan (213,799 insns) confirms zero stores to 0x801212e4.
          → analysis/reverse_engineering_sub_installers.md (revised)
          → analysis/reverse_engineering_hardware_layer.md (Section 7 revised)

          Sub-installer RUNTIME addresses (from literal pool, corrected):
            sub-call #1: 0x8010B254  (file offset 0xB254 — BEYOND binary)
            sub-call #2: 0x8010F7C8  (file offset 0xF7C8 — BEYOND binary)
            sub-call #3: 0x8010F304  (file offset 0xF304 — BEYOND binary)
            sub-call #4: 0x8010EA1C  (file offset 0xEA1C — BEYOND binary)
            sub-call #5: 0x8010E8A8  (file offset 0xE8A8 — BEYOND binary)
          (GZF data block uses different addresses: 8010af40, 8011011c, etc.
           — Kovah's runtime snapshot, different firmware variant)

[DONE]  Analyze sub-installers #1–#5 via GZF DATA block (2026-06-08)
          6 functions decompiled:
          #1 FUN_8010af40 — clears bit 6 of HW reg 0x108
          #2 FUN_8011011c — installs 19 fn-ptrs into 0x80120600-0x80121100
          #3 FUN_8010fc58 — installs 1 fn-ptr (FUN_80110ca4) + calls another
          #4 FUN_8010f370 — installs 10 data-ptrs into a struct (0x28 bytes)
          #5 FUN_8010e81c — installs 1 fn-ptr (FUN_8010e82c)
          #6 FUN_8010eac0 — writes 0xffffffff to global + calls via ptr
          → analysis/reverse_engineering_sub_installers.md

[DONE]  Analyze second-tier installer
          patch_that_installs_all_the_string_associated_function_patches__including_LMP
          CORRECTION (2026-06-08): Earlier analysis was WRONG. The installer is
          NOT the address-pair table — it is FUN_8010e27c (runtime 0x8010e27c),
          a 52-byte function that directly installs 6 protocol dispatch handlers
          by writing fn-ptrs to fixed struct offsets (base: 0x8012ae8c).
          Called by ROM 0x80009990 hook mechanism (not table processor).
          Also programs 3 BB registers (0x40/0x6b/0x6c) during installation.
          → analysis/reverse_engineering_string_assoc_installer.md (revised)
          → analysis/reverse_engineering_protocol_dispatch_layer.md (new)

          6 protocol dispatch handlers installed:
            struct[+0x48] → FUN_8010dfb0 (530B) assoc_w_tLMP:
              handles opcodes 0x480/0x489 (SSP), 0x270 (eSCO link), 0x259/0x26f
            struct[+0x00] → FUN_8010cc94 ( 26B) unknown_fptr_index0:
              pre-hook + original handler sequencing
            struct[+0x3c] → FUN_8010da70 ( 44B) assoc_w_tLC_TX:
              intercepts LC TX opcode 0x32e (eSCO codec TX)
            struct[+0x18] → FUN_8010d9f4 ( 98B) assoc_w_tLC_RX:
              intercepts LC RX opcode 0x2cd (eSCO codec RX)
            struct[+0x30] → FUN_8010daa4 (518B) assoc_w_tHCI_EVT:
              intercepts HCI events: 0xe (cmd_complete+scan), 0x1 (inquiry_cmplt+AFH),
              0x3 (conn_cmplt), 0x3e (LE meta), 0x5/0x4/0x14 (disc/auth/role), etc.
            struct[+0x60] → FUN_8010d154 ( 16B) assoc_w_tLMP_CH__passthrough:
              pure passthrough to ROM

          Also decompiled 7 late-patch functions (see below).


PHASE 2 — LATE-PATCH FUNCTIONS (decompiled 2026-06-08)
---------------------------------------------------------
[DONE]  FUN_80009980 (runtime 0x80109980, size=175) — HW register init
          Uses ROM register-read (thunk → FUN_8000a180 → ROM 0x8001136c) and
          register-write (ROM 0x8001139c) fns. Programs 7 baseband registers
          (indices 0,2,3,5,6). Reads eSCO codec params from bos+0x168/0x16a.
          MMIO base: physical 0x1000a0bc (kseg1: 0xb000a0bc).
[DONE]  FUN_80009c08 (runtime 0x80109c08, size=448) — eSCO negotiator
          Selects eSCO packet type from connection type (0xA000/0xB000/0xE000/0xF000)
          and capability flags at conn_rec+0x250. Returns type code (0x3/0x4/0x8/
          0xa/0xb/0x3a-0x4b). Calls ROM selector fn and two alternate paths.
[DONE]  FUN_80009de0 (runtime 0x80109de0, size=164) — Hamming-weight checksum
          Standard popcount over first 10 bytes of input. Returns 8-bit bit-count.
          Likely used for LMP PDU header validation.
[DONE]  FUN_80009200 (runtime 0x80109200, size=322) — Bitfield encoder
          Reads packed 2-bit groups from array, constructs 16-bit register values,
          programs hardware via fn pointers. Likely PCM/I2S or RF init.
[DONE]  FUN_80009550 (runtime 0x80109550, size=226) — Audio codec sampler
          64-iteration loop reading codec samples; passes to debug logger.
[DONE]  FUN_800096d4 (runtime 0x801096d4, size=258) — Audio circular buffer writer
          8-element circular buffer, 12-byte frames, two write modes (SCO parity).
[DONE]  FUN_80009824 (runtime 0x80109824, size=180) — eSCO retransmission timer
          Checks packet counter vs threshold; handles retry and teardown logic.
[DONE]   MIPS16e handler stubs @ 0x8010A160-0x8010A280 (2026-06-08)
          RESOLVED — misidentification. The "stubs" are the CODE BODY of FUN_8010a000
          (patch entry, 578 bytes). GZF DATA BLOCK correctly decoded by Ghidra; the
          repeating 8-byte bteqz/lw/bteqz/addiu pattern is FUN_8010a000's MIPS16e
          comparison logic (parameter checks + case branches). Literal pool starts at
          0x8010a244. Old import mode failed due to EXTEND pcode errors without full
          memory context; GZF PROCESS MODE resolves correctly.
          Address-pair table at file 0xa0 (fn_ptrs 0x8010A174/A184/A1D8/A208/A2B8/
          A304/A34C) → these fn_ptrs point INTO FUN_8010a000's code body, NOT to
          standalone handler entry points. Table purpose UNRESOLVED (separate from
          the 6 protocol handlers above; fn_ptrs lack MIPS16e prologues).
          → analysis/reverse_engineering_string_assoc_installer.md (revised)


PHASE 3 — UNDERSTAND THE HARDWARE LAYER
-----------------------------------------
[DONE]  Decompile the hardware-write hook installed at 0x801212e4 (2026-06-09)
          RESOLVED — not a single decompilable patch function. Two distinct +0xe4
          mechanisms clarified via FUN_80025b68 + FUN_8004f824 decompile
          (AnalyzeHwWriteHook.java, GZF process mode):
          (A) GLOBAL hook slot 0x801212e4 (bos_base+0xe4): read by ROM FUN_8004f824
              via PTR_DAT_8004f890. Zero stores in patch OR ROM → stays NULL in GZF
              snapshot. When NULL, FUN_8004f824 runs slot-budget clamp only (no HW
              register writes). Libre: leave NULL — no stub required.
          (B) PER-CONNECTION hook crypto_struct+0xe4: written by ROM FUN_80025b68
              at 0x80025bb0 → points to crypto_struct+0x13e (same conn's code buf).
              Template MIPS16e (0x30 codec-6 / 0x40 codec-8) copied from ROM staging
              tables PTR_DAT_80025ca8/cac with half-reversal unscramble. Triggered
              during SSP IO-cap exchange (not SCO setup). Position-dependent code —
              branch at +0x0c exits buffer; cannot decompile in isolation.
          Codec-6 h0 unscrambled first insns: cmpi v1,0x6f; sb s0,0x19(a1); swsp…
          FUN_80024218 post-install: conditional LMP__268 patch-gateway call.
          CONCLUSION: Libre firmware needs ZERO implementation for either hook path.
          → analysis/reverse_engineering_hardware_layer.md (Section 12 added)

[DONE]  Analyze hardware register read/write functions (2026-06-08)
          ROM 0x8001136c (read): index in bits[21:16], returns bits[15:0].
          ROM 0x8001139c (write): same index encoding; two MMIO writes (value,
          then value|trigger_bit) to latch. MMIO addr: 0xb000a0bc (phys 0x1000a0bc).
          FUN_8000a180: NOT a simple thunk — is a retry/polling wrapper around the
          read fn; called from FUN_80009980 via v0 fn-ptr.
          → analysis/reverse_engineering_rom_regs.md (new)

[DONE]  Read ROM codec templates PTR_DAT_80025ca8 / PTR_DAT_80025cac (2026-06-08)
          PTR_DAT_80025ca8 → RAM 0x8012205c (codec-6 staging base)
          PTR_DAT_80025cac → RAM 0x801220ec (codec-8 staging base)
          ROM source bytes: codec-6 h0 at 0x80079f0c, h1 at 0x80079be0,
          h2a at 0x80079ef4, h2b at 0x80079c10; codec-8 h0 at 0x8007a07c,
          h1 at 0x80079c28, h2a at 0x8007a05c, h2b at 0x80079c68.
          Staging tables initialized by ROM FUN_800225a8 (called by FUN_800614fc).
          Un-scramble algorithm: two independent half-reversals (FUN_80025b68).
          Templates are position-dependent code: branch at +0x0c exits buffer.
          CONCLUSION: 100% ROM-managed. Libre firmware needs ZERO implementation.
          → analysis/reverse_engineering_hardware_layer.md (Section 9)

[DONE]  Confirm what invokes ROM FUN_80025b68 (2026-06-08)
          CORRECTION: FUN_80025b68 is triggered during SSP (Secure Simple Pairing)
          IO capability exchange — NOT SCO/eSCO audio setup as previously thought.
          Three ROM callers identified:
            ROM LMP_encryption_opcode_handlers @ 0x80028264
              → FUN_80029364 @ 0x80029364  [state==0x15 → FUN_80025b68]
              → FUN_800293f0 @ 0x800293f0  [state==0x1d → FUN_80025b68]
            ROM HCI_Write_Simple_Pairing_Debug_Mode @ 0x800233e8
              → FUN_80023d14 @ 0x80023d14  → FUN_80025b68
          Second arg to FUN_80025b68 is role_bit (0=slave/1=master), not conn idx.
          Role bit selects which template variant is un-scrambled.
          All callers are ROM functions dispatched by ROM LMP/HCI state machine.
          CONCLUSION: Libre firmware needs ZERO additional wiring. Runs automatically.
          → analysis/reverse_engineering_hardware_layer.md (Section 9 updated)

[DONE]  Analyze ROM functions for connection types 0-3 (hw init chain) (2026-06-08)
          All five functions (FUN_80050810 + four handlers) are pure ROM.
          FUN_80050810: dispatches on param+0x08 bits[2:0] = connection type (0-3),
            then computes slot interval from 7-bit capability bitmask (param+0x0b)
            using DAT_8007abd8, stores in param+0x09.
          Type 0 (FUN_800506ac): new SCO/eSCO initiation; validates caps, allocates
            link slots via FUN_80050610 + FUN_800508f8; returns 5 on failure.
          Type 1 (FUN_8004e670): accept/mirror — copies cap flags from parent record.
          Type 2 (FUN_8004e6f4): renegotiation — adjusts caps from parent; SCO-only
            special case forces +0xb = 3.
          Type 3 (FUN_8004e76c): restore/reject — forces eSCO-only (bit 3 only).
          Override slot 0x801212e0 (checked first by FUN_80050810): can be NULL.
          CONCLUSION: Libre firmware needs ZERO implementation. ROM manages all of it.
          → analysis/reverse_engineering_hardware_layer.md (Section 10 added)

[DONE]  Read eSCO packet-type tables (2026-06-08)
          FUN_80044730 (ROM, 102 bytes): takes 16-bit packet-type code at param_1+4,
            computes index = code - 0x10 (valid 0x10..0x1d, 14 entries).
          Table A @ 0x8007abb0: validity — 0x00=OK, 0x12=unsupported.
            Valid codes: 0x10, 0x12, 0x13, 0x15, 0x1d.
          Table B @ 0x8007abc0: codec-type 3-bit selector stored into param_2+0x1d
            bits[7:5]. Codec values: 0=µ-law/linear, 1=A-law, 2=CVSD, 3=transparent,
            4=vendor/wideband.
          Callers (0x80047ca6, 0x80047edc) are both ROM.
          Confirmed: DAT_8007abd8 (slot interval table for FUN_80050810) lies
            immediately after these tables in ROM at 0x8007abd8 = 06 06 01 02 03 12 01.
          CONCLUSION: 100% ROM. Libre firmware needs ZERO implementation.
          → analysis/reverse_engineering_hardware_layer.md (Section 11 added)

[DONE]  Analyze early-init function FUN_8010a6c8 (2026-06-08)
          24-byte BSS-zeroing stub. Calls ROM memset(0x80109c00, 0, 0x400) via
          literal-pool pointer 0x8000e98d (MIPS16e). Zeroes exactly 1 KB of
          patch RAM before any hooks are installed.
          Confirms patch RAM layout:
            0x80100000-0x80109bff: code section 1 (master installer, hooks)
            0x80109c00-0x80109fff: BSS / zero-init data  ← what this fn clears
            0x8010a000-0x8010adc3: code section 2 (entry point, late fns)
          Callers: master installer at 0x379c (28 bytes in) AND
                   patch entry FUN_8010a000 at 0x8010a01c.
          0x8010a000 used as the end-ptr confirms it IS the patch entry base.
          LIBRE: trivial — zero file offsets 0x9c00-0x9fff OR call ROM memset.
          → analysis/reverse_engineering_patch_installer.md (Appendix added)

[DONE]  Analyze patch entry point FUN_8010a000 (2026-06-08)
          578-byte MONOLITHIC installer — NOT a thin wrapper. Is the true entry.
          ROM caller: calls_to_0x8010a001_as_fptr_to_install_patches @ 0x80010a18
            (COMPUTED_CALL to 0x8010a001, MIPS16e odd addr).
          Does: config copy → BSS init → 35+ hook installs → 6 sub-installers →
            copies_config_bdaddr (ROM 0x8000fd38) → chip-rev version check →
            conditional extra hw init → write 4 to "patch active" global.
          FUN_80103780 is NOT called — they are parallel variants from different
            GZF memory blocks (patch block vs data block).
          Chip-rev check: table at PTR_DAT_8010a3a0[0..15] → bool flag; gates
            additional hw init for specific silicon revisions.
          Callees still unknown: FUN_8010a7b8, FUN_8010ad38, FUN_8010b04c,
            FUN_8010e214, FUN_8010c278, ROM FUN_8003aea0.
          → analysis/reverse_engineering_patch_installer.md (new section appended)

[DONE]  Analyze unknown entry callees (2026-06-08)
          All 6 callees of FUN_8010a000 decompiled. ALL are mandatory.
          FUN_8010a7b8  (114 B) — TLV config applier: iterates TLV-encoded config blob,
            applies records as memcpy patches to config_base + record_type offset.
          FUN_8010ad38   (66 B) — HW variant probe: reads HW fields 0x120/0x124 via
            ROM FUN_80011510; bitmask check gates chip-specific init paths.
          FUN_8010b04c   (72 B) — Baseband reg init: programs regs 0x114 (sets bits 0,1)
            and 0x154 (RMW with literal-pool mask+OR) via ROM read/write fn-ptrs.
          FUN_8010e214   (96 B) — Silicon revision detector: writes mode bit, reads HW
            fields 0x7e/0x7f via ROM FUN_8000b820; extracts 5-bit revision level 0-15;
            return value indexes PTR_DAT_8010a3a0 chip-rev table. Returns 0xff=unknown.
          FUN_8010c278  (394 B) — RF channel init: calls variant selector (0-6), loads
            one of 7 register tables, clears bit 8 of each listed register. 14-26 entries
            per table. Calls ROM FUN_80011584 (read) + FUN_80011608 (write).
          ROM FUN_8003aea0 (688 B) — Register script interpreter: 16-opcode dispatch
            on high nibble of cmd word; executes (ptr,count) reg-cmd arrays; called
            from 15+ ROM+patch sites. PURE ROM — libre calls via ROM addr, no reimpl.
          → analysis/reverse_engineering_patch_installer.md (Appendix B added)

[DONE]  Identify register-table data for FUN_8010c278 (RF channel init) (2026-06-08)
          FUN_8010c260 (20 B): reads ROM reg 0xfd via ROM FUN_800115c8, returns bits[2:0]
            = RF hardware variant 0-6. New ROM fn: FUN_800115c8 (RF reg-read interface).
          7 RF register tables: contiguous packed region 0x8011106c-0x80111185 (280 bytes)
            in DATA block. All contain uint16 RF register indices in range 0x0160-0x01f0.
            Each case: memcpy table to stack, iterate clearing bit 8 of each register.
            Literal pool at 0x8010c410-0x8010c438: fn-ptrs at c410/c414/c41c/c420,
            table ptrs at c418/c424/c428/c42c/c430/c434/c438 (non-contiguous in pool).
          VERDICT: ALL 7 TABLES SAFE TO COPY VERBATIM — pure hardware config constants,
            no code, no computed values, no pointers. Chip design data.
          FUN_8003aea0 call from entry: 2-entry reg-cmd array at ROM-initialized RAM
            0x80120264 → [cmd=0x80a6, val=2] + [cmd=0xffff, val=0xffff].
            fn-ptr at 0x801205b4 → 0x8003aea1 (ROM FUN_8003aea0 confirmed).
            Data at 0x80120264 is ROM-pre-populated; libre firmware calls via fn-ptr,
            no data needs embedding.
          → analysis/reverse_engineering_patch_installer.md (Appendix C added)

[DONE]  Analyze FUN_8010a7b8 (TLV config applier) in full detail (2026-06-08)
          Scripts: DataBlockAnalysis.java + DumpEntryLiteralPool.java
          RESOLVED — complete literal pool + full decompile:
            config_base = RAM 0x80120070 (ROM-initialized; "RRTK_BT_5.0" at +0x49)
            TLV blob: start=0x801115f8, magic@0x801115fc=0x8723ab55, count@0x80111600
            TLV entries: 0x80111602-0x80113fff (~40KB available)
            Apply fn: ROM optimized_memcpy @ 0x8000e85c
            In DATA snapshot: remaining=0 (no active TLV records; function is a no-op)
            LIBRE: Can skip TLV loop by leaving remaining=0; config_base is ROM-initialized
          All 44 fn-ptr hook installs in FUN_8010a000 enumerated with exact RAM slots:
            44 direct installs targeting 0x80120xxx-0x80126xxx RAM slots
            6 sub-installer calls (FUN_8010af40/fc58/f370/e81c/eac0 + FUN_8011011c)
            ROM calls: FUN_8003aea0, copies_config_bdaddr, FUN_8010c278
            Conditional: FUN_8010ad38 probe → FUN_8010b04c (chip-rev gated)
          New functions identified: FUN_8010ce0c/fa34/f950/fb08/e350/bda0/c09c/b4d0
          → analysis/reverse_engineering_patch_installer.md (Appendix D+E added)

[DONE]  Analyze remaining small functions in DATA block 0xa000 region (2026-06-08)
          10 + 5 = 15 functions decompiled. Only 2 are trivial stubs; 13 require real code.
          KEY FINDINGS:
            FUN_8010a49c (10B) — trivial: *(0x8012b803) = 0
            FUN_8010a594 (14B) — trivial: *(0xb6001080) = 0x80
            FUN_8010a410 (86B) — HW reg 0x11C configurator (eSCO codec mode bits)
            FUN_8010a4ac (68B) — eSCO readiness gate (6-condition check)
            FUN_8010a550 (54B) — Set eSCO-active flag
            FUN_8010a5ac (36B) — Timing compensation adder (stride-0x1ac struct)
            FUN_8010a5d8 (94B) — Codec reg 0x1FE configurator (MMIO 0xb000a030/0xb60010ce)
            FUN_8010a6ec (180B) — eSCO slot buffer allocator (uses ROM table 0x8007abd8)
            FUN_8010a84c (450B) — SCO/eSCO connection response handler (10+ ROM calls)
            FUN_8010aa58 (96B) — SCO connection continuation handler (phase 2)
            FUN_8010b118 (82B) — Slot interval allocator (ROM 0x80056609/56661)
            FUN_8010b3d8 (206B) — ACL slot scheduler (interrupt-protected, residual calc)
            FUN_8010b0a4 (108B) — ACL packet type flag corrector (MMIO 0xb6001214)
            FUN_8010c780 (34B) — Subsystem initializer (calls 3 fns + sets flag)
            FUN_8010c63c (278B) — Retransmission counter / ACL packet handler
          → analysis/reverse_engineering_sco_esco_layer.md (new)
          New unknown fn: FUN_80110869 (called by FUN_8010c780, in DATA block)

[DONE]  Analyze FUN_80110869 + 8 hook targets from FUN_8010a84c pool (2026-06-08)
          Scripts: DecompileNewHookFns.java + DecompileHookFnsBatch.java
          ALL 9 functions are REAL — none trivial. Key findings:
          FUN_80110868 (322B) — eSCO codec frame ring-buffer scheduler (8-slot, stride 0x10)
            Infinite loop flushing pending codec frames; two modes (encode/decode paths)
          FUN_8010ce0c (728B) — AFH capability mapper: scatters ch_class bits into HW cap
            register; programs BB regs 0x15c/0x1fc; calls AFH init chain (4 tail-calls)
          FUN_8010fa34 (184B) — AFH 79-ch map merger: AND local+remote, enforce min 20
          FUN_8010f950 (174B) — AFH channel quality handler + VSC fc95 "start scan" trigger
          FUN_8010fb08 (292B) — BLE 40-ch map aggregator: AND 3 maps, min 2, failure count
          FUN_8010e350 (1174B) — AFH quality ranking engine: rank 79 channels, pick top N≥20,
            apply HW forbidden mask, enforce min after masking
          FUN_8010bda0 (114B) — SCO/eSCO acceptance validator: reject (LMP 0xe/err 0x12)
            if conn flags wrong, else update conn record
          FUN_8010c09c (76B) — per-link capability gate: clears bits 2-8,12-13 of BB reg 0xf
          FUN_8010b4d0 (76B) — eSCO slot allocation trigger: stores cap data, fires conn;
            UNRESOLVED tail-call indirect jump at end
          → analysis/reverse_engineering_sco_esco_layer.md (Group C added)
          New unknowns: 4 AFH init tail-calls from ce0c (DAT_8010d140/d144/d14c/d150)
                        + unresolved jumptable in b4d0

[DONE]  Identify the 4 AFH init tail-call functions from FUN_8010ce0c literal pool (2026-06-08)
          Scripts: ResolveAFHPtrs.java + DecompileAFHInitFns.java + DumpCCB8Pool.java +
                   DecompileAFHHelpers.java + DumpAD88Pool.java
          RESOLVED:
            DAT_8010d140 → FUN_800117a4 (ROM, 14B): ORs 0xfc00 into global (AFH mask enable)
            DAT_8010d144 → FUN_8000c3f4 (ROM, 414B): AFH channel map updater
            DAT_8010d148 → DAT_80121908 (data label): struct base, zeroed at +0x40 (not a fn)
            DAT_8010d14c → FUN_800122b8 (ROM, 64B): AFH cap extractor (arg=1 → bits[11:8])
            DAT_8010d150 → FUN_8010ccb8 (PATCH, 264B): AFH HW reg configurator ← NEEDS IMPL
          FUN_8010b4d0 literal pool resolved (b4d0 = eSCO slot allocation trigger):
            0x8010b5b8 → base_of_0x1ac_struct_array_0xA_large2[1].field0_0x0 (data)
            0x8010b5bc → base_of_0x1ac_struct_array_0xA_large2 (data)
            0x8010b5c0 → send_evt_HCI_Read_Remote_Version_Information_Complete (ROM, 134B)
            0x8010b5c8 → access_config_at_0xa5_and_0x1ac_stuct_stuff (ROM, 118B)
            0x8010b5cc → assign_pointer_to_0x1AC_offset_0x134 (ROM, 88B)
            0x8010b5d0 → FUN_8005ca00 (ROM, 48B): set bit in capacity bitmask
            UNRESOLVED: tail-call at end of b4d0 — Ghidra "Too many branches" at 0x8010b5b4
          New PATCH functions found: FUN_8010ccb8 (264B) + FUN_8010ad88 (40B)
          New ROM fns: FUN_80011510, FUN_80011608, FUN_80011a74, FUN_800122b8, FUN_80012e38,
                       FUN_800117a4, FUN_8000c3f4, FUN_8001d4a0, FUN_8005e23c, FUN_8005d26c,
                       FUN_8005ca00
          → analysis/reverse_engineering_sco_esco_layer.md (Group D added)

[DONE]  Resolve FUN_8010b4d0 unresolved tail-call (2026-06-08)
          RESOLVED — FALSE ALARM. The "UNRECOVERED_JUMPTABLE" at 0x8010b5b4 is simply
          `jr a3` = standard MIPS16e function return. Full epilogue:
            8010b5ae: lw a3, 0x24(sp)   ; restore saved ra (was: sw ra,0x24(sp) in prologue)
            8010b5b0: lw s1, 0x20(sp)   ; restore s1
            8010b5b2: lw s0, 0x1c(sp)   ; restore s0
            8010b5b4: jr a3             ; RETURN (Ghidra lost track that a3=saved ra)
            8010b5b6: addiu sp, 0x28    ; delay-slot: restore stack
          The 8 bytes `49 e3 40 f2 74 aa 8c eb` (at 0x8010b514-0x8010b51b) are the last
          bytes of the 76-byte function body: addu + lhu v1,0x254(v0) + and — normal ops.
          The value 0x6305ef00 at 0x8010b5b4 is two MIPS16e instruction words (jr + addiu).
          FUN_8010b4d0 is FULLY RESOLVED — no switch table, no indirect jump.

          COMPLETE DECOMPILE (from AnalyzeB4D0Tail.java via GZF process mode):
          Function: void FUN_8010b4d0(int cap_pdu, undefined4 p2, uint conn_idx)
          - param_3 (conn_idx) &= 0xff; offset = conn_idx * 0x1ac
          - conn_rec = large2_base_8010b5b8 + offset   (0x80123a20-based array)
          - Copies cap_pdu fields into conn_rec: +0x3c (byte), +0x3e (u16), +0x40 (u16)
          - Sets conn_rec+0x90 bit 1 ("pending")
          - If cap_flags[conn]+0x254 bit 1 set: call cancel_fn (ROM 0x8001d4a0,odd), clear bit
          - If not-active (conn_rec+0x90 & 1 == 0):
              If no timers (conn_rec+0x7c==0 && +0x78==0):
                conn_rec+0x7c = 0x20; call (**0x8012082c)(conn_idx, 6); set active bit
                ts = ROM FUN_8005e23c(); ROM FUN_8005d26c(ts, conn_idx)
                ROM FUN_8005ca00(conn_rec, 0xc, 2); update conn_rec+0x8f bit4
              else: conn_rec+0x8f |= 0x10
          - else (already active): call (**0x80120958)(conn_rec, 0x20, 1)
          - return

          TWO NEW LITERAL POOL ENTRIES (previously missed):
            0x8010b5c4 → 0x8012082c  RAM fn-ptr slot (double-indirect call)
            0x8010b5d4 → 0x80120958  RAM fn-ptr slot (double-indirect call)
          FULL POOL: b5b8=0x80123a20 (struct[1].f0), b5bc=0x8012382c (struct base),
            b5c0=0x8001d4a1 (ROM:cancel/send_HCI_event), b5c4=0x8012082c (ind fn ptr),
            b5c8=0x8005e23d (ROM:get_ts), b5cc=0x8005d26d (ROM:record_ts),
            b5d0=0x8005ca01 (ROM:set_cap_bit), b5d4=0x80120958 (ind fn ptr)
          NEW function FUN_8010b5d8 starts immediately after the literal pool.
          → analysis/reverse_engineering_sco_esco_layer.md (FUN_8010b4d0 section updated)


[DONE]  Decompile FUN_8010b5d8 + FUN_8010b64c + ROM pair (2026-06-08)

                   DecompileRomPair.java
          FUN_8010b5d8 (100B) — eSCO connection activator:
            Sets conn_rec+0x90|=1 (active), calls ROM access_config+assign_pointer,
            sets conn_rec+0x78|=0x20, clears +0x8f bit 4, calls **0x8012082c(conn_idx,6),

          FUN_8010b64c (344B) — LMP eSCO link request initiator:
            Looks up conn by handle (ROM lookup_up_to_3_bos...), validates eSCO packet
            type from table@0x80111198, builds LMP opcode 0x25 (LMP_eSCO_link_req) PDU
            with params from config_base+0xa4 and DAT_80120060, sends via send_LMP_pkt,
            marks opcode 0x26 pending, sends HCI Command Status, then either calls
            FUN_8010b5d8 directly or sets deferred flag at conn_rec+0x8f|=0x10.

[DONE]  Decompile FUN_8010bb54 (2026-06-08)

PHASE 7 — TEST
---------------
[DONE]  Diagnose FC20 timeout on TP-Link UB500 (0x2357:0x0604) (2026-06-09)
          User report: `command 0xfc20 tx timeout` / `download fw command failed (-110)`
          after driver loaded libre fw (cfg_sz 6, total sz 27814). Root cause:
          patch_entry was linked at PRAM+0 (runtime 0x8010A000) but ROM loads the
          EPatch body at 0x80103780 and calls 0x8010A001 (+0x6880). Our code landed
          at 0x80103780 → ROM jumped to wrong address → hang → HCI timeout.
          FIX (rebuilt 2026-06-09):
            rtl8761bu.ld: load base 0x80103780; helpers in .text/.text.hooks;
              thin patch_entry stub in .text.entry @ +0x6880 (28 B budget).
            init.S: patch_entry_body holds installer; entry calls it.
            pad.py: NOP-fill pre-entry gap to exactly 0x6880 bytes.
            pack.py: 8-byte Realtech header per struct rtl_epatch_header
              (14 B); fw_version 0x09a98a6b. 9-byte Realtechk was wrong —
              shifted num_patches → "didn't find patch for chip id 1".
          Build: 4748 B code / 27808 B PRAM (3.7% free), verify OK.
          entry@+6880 = ff630162 (MIPS16e prologue). User should retest.
[BLOCKED]  Flash libre patch to UB500 dongle via btrtl driver (2026-06-09)
          No UB500 dongle in dev container; user has TP-Link UB500 on NeoPC host.
          Install rebuilt blobs:
            sudo cp rtl8761bu-libre/rtl8761bu_fw.bin /lib/firmware/rtl_bt/
            sudo cp rtl8761bu-libre/rtl8761bu_config.bin /lib/firmware/rtl_bt/
          Unplug/replug or `rmmod btusb && modprobe btusb`.
          Success dmesg: fw version 0x09a98a6b, NO fc20 timeout.
[DONE]  Fix FC20 timeout round 2 (2026-06-09)
          After header fix, still fc20 timeout. Changes:
            pack.py: dual-patch layout (42,088 B, matches non-free); 8-byte Realtech.
            make minimal: P0 entry (patch-active flag only) for smoke test.
            init.S: zero 0x80120f0c/0x80120c80 before sub-inst #3/#6 indirect calls

Implementation order (summary):
  8.0 compliance gates → 8.1 prefix finish → 8.2 T1 hooks + dispatch →
  P1 hardware → 8.3 T2 eSCO → P2 SHIP → 8.4 T3 AFH → 8.5 P4 parity.


PHASE 9 — COMPLETE REVERSING AND DOCUMENTATION OF THE ROM (SECONDARY, NICE-TO-HAVE)
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Goal: build a complete, documented understanding of the RTL8761BU mask ROM
(0x80000000-0x8007ffff, 512 KB) for research/educational value. Unlike Phases
1-8, this has NO shipping deliverable — the ROM is fixed in chip silicon and
can never be reflashed on real hardware. Lower priority than the primary
firmware goal; ongoing/best-effort rather than a ship gate. Findings live in
analysis/rom/ (see analysis/INDEX.md for the index + the rule on adding to it).

[DONE]  Incidental ROM RE carried over from Phases 1-8 (not re-done here)
          Four ROM subsystems already fully documented as a side effect of
          building the libre firmware's hook map:
            analysis/rom/reverse_engineering_hardware_layer.md — FUN_8004f824
              slot-budget validator + 7-entry interval table
            analysis/rom/reverse_engineering_vsc_dispatcher.md — FUN_80047c50
              VSC parameter validator + connection record writer
            analysis/rom/reverse_engineering_conn_record_subsystem.md — eSCO/SCO
              connection record pool (alloc/register/lookup/commit/free)
            analysis/rom/reverse_engineering_rom_regs.md — HW register r/w
              protocol (0x8001136c/9c, MMIO 0xb000a0bc)
          Also: kovah_function_list.md's ROM section is the starting name index.

[DONE]  Baseline current ROM coverage (2026-06-21)
          Ran RomCoverageStats.java + RomNamedFuncAddrs.java (both scripts
          pre-existed in GHIDRA_SCRIPTS.md) against the GZF rom block. Result:
          2738 total functions, 461 user-named (16.84%); 95.37% of ROM bytes
          defined (instructions+data) vs 4.63% undefined; only 16.99% of ROM
          bytes fall inside a *named* function. Written up in
          analysis/rom/rom_coverage_baseline.md (indexed in analysis/INDEX.md).

            analysis/rom/reverse_engineering_baseband_reg_helpers.md — 9 fns:

            analysis/rom/reverse_engineering_conn_feature_dispatch.md — 10 fns:
              FUN_80056988, FUN_8004f25c, FUN_800511b8, FUN_80050b2c,
              FUN_80050ff8, FUN_8004f374, FUN_80052c1c, FUN_8004e808,
              FUN_80051124, FUN_8004e2d0
            analysis/rom/reverse_engineering_register_script_interpreter.md —

[DONE]  Map the boot / reset sequence (2026-06-21)
          Found and documented analysis/rom/reverse_engineering_boot_reset_sequence.md:
          a 32-bit MIPS (not MIPS16e!) boot preamble at ROM base 0x80000000-
          ~0x800000c8, previously totally undocumented (not in
          kovah_function_list.md, no Kovah annotations). Confirmed: MMIO pokes
          at 0xb000af08/0xb000a000, CP0 Status read-mask-write (clear boot-
          exception-vector bit, set IM mask) -- the closest thing to a
          documented reset-vector handler this chip has. Confirmed the
          ROM->patch-entry call chain (0x800109ac calls 0x8010a001) is a
          *separate*, patch-download-time event, not part of power-on boot.
          Open: ~36KB gap (0x800000c8-0x80009104) not walked -- presumably
          contains the MIPS16e mode switch (jalx) and any watchdog/clock init;
          lots_of_initialization (0x8000fb5c) located but not decompiled.
          Documented as future work, not blockers.
          Also found and documented a wairz bug: save_ghidra_script overwrites
          of an existing script filename do not take effect on subsequent
          run_ghidra_headless script_name executions (stale content keeps
          running) -- see "Tool note" section in the new doc for repro.

[DONE]  Map the interrupt vector table and ISR handlers (2026-06-21)
          Found and documented analysis/rom/reverse_engineering_interrupt_vectors.md.
          No classical fixed vector table exists (all conventional BEV=0
          offsets 0x80/0x100/0x180/0x200 and BEV=1 0xbfc0xxxx addresses
          checked -- the latter unmapped, the former just ordinary
          unremarkable code, not vector stubs). Instead found a single fixed
          context-save trampoline at 0x80009160 (32-bit MIPS): saves all
          GPRs+HI/LO/EPC to a k0-relative RAM frame, then jalr's to
          0x80033ce9 (odd addr = MIPS16e call target) -- this resolved the
          boot-reset doc's open "where's the jalx mode-switch" question (a
          concrete jalx 0x80009014 instance found in
          calls_to_0x8010a001_as_fptr_to_install_patches). The MIPS16e
          dispatcher FUN_80033ce8 is a single-slot ISR dispatcher: calls a
          registered fptr (PTR_DAT_80033d1c, default 0x80120f84, in the
          bos_base RAM region) or falls back to acking via MMIO word
          0xb000a0a0 -- confirmed sibling register to the documented HW port
          0xb000a0bc (same 0xb000a0xx control-register block), answering the
          ticket's HW-MMIO-relation question. Also corrected an error in the
          boot-reset doc: disable_interrupts/enable_interrupts (0x80009104/
          0x80009120) are 32-bit MIPS (mfc0/mtc0), not MIPS16e as that doc
          claimed.
          Open (documented, not blocking): exact silicon trap PC unconfirmed
          (0x80009160 is the strongest candidate, not proven); restore path
          at 0x80009220 not individually re-disassembled (inferred by
          symmetry); single-slot-vs-table ambiguity for real interrupt
          sources not resolved; 0xb000a0a0 bit semantics inferred from access
          pattern only, not a datasheet.
          Tool limitation hit and flagged per CLAUDE.md (not worked around):
          BOTH wairz script-storage pools were full -- the research-files
          pool (save_ghidra_script/script_file_id) at exactly 50/50 with no
          delete/evict tool, AND the separate scripts-directory pool
          (script_name, GHIDRA_SCRIPTS.md) also at 50, which
          save_ghidra_script cannot write to anyway (confirmed via backend
          source read). Could not create the planned new batch probe script;
          worked around by using pre-existing DiagAddr.java/DecompileAddr.java
          one-address-at-a-time instead. See new doc's "Tool note" section.

[DONE]  Document the full HCI command parser / router (2026-06-21)
          Found and fully decompiled the top-level standard-HCI dispatcher
          assoc_w_tHCI_CMD (0x80020ee0, 672B): housekeeping, raw-opcode
          special cases (0x300/0x456/0x1), loopback-mode short-circuit,
          HCI_Reset-while-busy disconnect guard, OGF = opcode>>10 extraction
          (confirmed the OGF/OCF bit layout generalizes beyond the
          already-documented OGF 0x3F case), an optional top-level
          pre-dispatch patch hook (PTR_PTR_800211a4), a debug var-args
          logger, then a linear (not jump-table) compare chain over OGF.
          All 8 standard OGF groups (0x01-0x08) now have confirmed handler
          addresses: OGF 1/2/3/5/6 were already named in
          kovah_function_list.md (confirmed reachable via direct jal sites);
          OGF 4 (Informational Parameters, 0x8002013c, 74B) and OGF 8 (LE
          Commands, 0x80044674, 176B) are NEW finds this pass, not in
          kovah_function_list.md before now -- both fully decompiled.
          OGF 4 is a near-stub that validates OCF range then delegates to
          the shared OGC_3_OCF_TONS_deal_with_return_status... sink. OGF 8
          has the same "extract OCF, log, bounds-check, jump-table" shape as
          OGF 3/6's big-switch dispatchers, but its jump table
          (PTR_PTR_8004472c) has exactly ONE live entry (OCF=0) pointing at
          an empty RAM hook slot (0x801206ac), not ROM code -- i.e. this ROM
          ships essentially no native LE command support, gated behind
          config_base+0x7a bit 0x2 (an already-documented config-blob
          feature flag, reused here as an LE-enable bit). Confirms OGF 0x07
          has NO case at all (only OGF 0x08 is LE, per spec -- the ticket's
          hedge about "0x08 per some specs" was unnecessary, spec is
          unambiguous and ROM matches it).
          Per-OGF OCF-level dispatch (the "real" jump tables) confirmed only
          for OGF 1 (872B, matches its 12 already-named OCF handlers),
          3, 6, 8; OGF 2/5 internals not walked (named addresses confirmed
          reachable, contents not decompiled -- left as documented open work).
          Wrote analysis/rom/reverse_engineering_hci_command_router.md;
          added row to INDEX.md; added OGF4/OGF8/assoc_w_tHCI_CMD entries to
          kovah_function_list.md. No wairz blocker this pass -- DiagAddr.java/
          DecompileAddr.java with 0x-prefixed script_args sufficed throughout
          (noted in the new doc: these two scripts need the 0x prefix,
          opposite of GHIDRA_SCRIPTS.md's general script_args hex-literal
          warning, which applies to a different invocation mode).

[DONE]  Document the link controller (LC) / LMP procedure state machine (2026-06-21)
          Baseband procedures beyond the eSCO/SCO/AFH paths already covered:
          inquiry, paging, role switch, authentication/pairing beyond the SSP
          IO-capability exchange (FUN_80025b68's *callers* are documented; the
          state machine that drives them is not), sniff/hold/park power modes.

          Traced from OGF1 (0x80020814)/OGF2 (0x8002060c) HCI handlers past the
          dispatch layer into actual baseband driver functions. Fully traced
          with addresses + decompiles: (1) Paging/HCI_Create_Connection --
          fHCI_Create_Connection_0x05 (0x8001bd38) allocates a conn-record slot
          then hands off via the shared dispatcher called_by_fHCI_Remote_
          Name_Request_5 (0x80036df8) to FUN_80041900 (0x80041900), which
          programs ~6 baseband HW registers (BD_ADDR-derived sync words, clock
          offset, page-timeout class) and sets the "paging in progress" flag.
          (2) Role switch/HCI_Switch_Role -- FUN_8001acd8 (0x8001acd8) ->
          FUN_8002143c feasibility check (already documented) -> FUN_8001ac74
          (0x8001ac74) kickoff/defer decision -> FUN_8001ab44 (0x8001ab44, newly
          decompiled this pass) computes a slot-offset/backoff and sends
          LMP_SLOT_OFFSET (opcode 0x13) via send_LMP_pkt (0x800611e4, confirmed
          as the ONE shared LMP-PDU-TX primitive used by every named LMP_*
          handler in kovah_function_list.md). Partially traced: (3) Inquiry --
          fHCI_Inquiry_0x01 (0x8001bfa0) trigger chain confirmed but the actual
          inquiry-train/FHS-broadcast logic not located. (4) Sniff -- only
          LMP_UNSNIFF_REQ exit-path (0x8001af9c) traced; HCI_Sniff_Mode entry
          not reached.
          Headline finding: there is no single monolithic LC/LMP "state
          machine" function -- architecture is one shared connection-record
          array + one shared send_LMP_pkt TX primitive + small per-procedure
          driver functions, with state tracked via a status byte (+0xb2) and
          several flag fields (+0x171/+0x16f/+0x179/+0xd0/+0x216) on the
          connection record.
          Explicitly unexplored (listed as future work in the new doc):
          inquiry-train/page-train low-level transmit loops (likely timer/
          interrupt-driven, outside the synchronous HCI-command call chain),
          HCI_Sniff_Mode entry, Hold mode, Park mode, the LMP PDU *receive-side*
          dispatcher that routes incoming LMP opcodes to handlers like
          LMP_encryption_opcode_handlers (the highest-value remaining target --
          would be the true receive-side counterpart to send_LMP_pkt), and the
          LMP_SWITCH_REQ PDU send itself (only its LMP_SLOT_OFFSET precursor
          was found).
          Wrote analysis/rom/reverse_engineering_lc_lmp_state_machine.md; added
          row to INDEX.md. No wairz blocker -- DiagAddr.java/DecompileAddr.java
          with 0x-prefixed script_args sufficed. New tool note (not a blocker,
          just documented for future sessions): mcp__wairz__xrefs_to does NOT
          work against this GZF filename (looks in a different binary store) --
          correctly avoided in favor of run_ghidra_headless per CLAUDE.md.

[DONE]  Document the BLE link layer state machine, if present in this ROM (2026-06-21)
          Advertising, scanning, and connection state machine. First confirm
          whether BLE link-layer logic actually lives in this ROM revision or
          is handled elsewhere, then document accordingly.

          Wrote analysis/rom/reverse_engineering_ble_link_layer.md; added row
          to INDEX.md. Conclusion: PARTIALLY IN ROM, with a correction to the
          prior HCI-router doc. (1) OGF8 LE *command parsing* is confirmed
          thin (1-entry OCF jump table -> ROM stub at 0x800454a8 that just
          echoes back HCI_Command_Status; prior doc's "no native LE command
          support" stands, though the RAM slot 0x801206ac is not literally
          "empty" -- it has ROM-default content, just an inert stub). (2) But
          a separate, large, fully-decompiled cluster of 17+ named
          send_evt_Meta_subevent_0x## functions (0x80044730-0x80046620+,
          rom block) generates nearly every LE Meta Event in the BT5.x spec
          -- Connection Complete/Enhanced Connection Complete (1032B, fully
          decompiled, reads conn handle/role/peer addr/interval/latency/
          timeout from the shared 0x1ac conn-record struct array also used
          by BT Classic SCO/eSCO), Advertising Report/Direct Advertising
          Report (332B, fully decompiled -- loops reports, copies BD_ADDR/
          RSSI/AD-payload), LTK Request, PHY Update Complete, Channel
          Selection Algorithm, LE Secure Connections P-256/DHKey pair, etc.
          This directly contradicts the prior doc's blanket "essentially no
          native LE support" framing -- that was only true for command
          parsing, not event generation. NOT found: a single monolithic
          link-layer *driver*/state-machine function that decides when to
          call these senders (the actual RF timing/anchor-point/channel-
          selection engine) -- searched via string search (FindStringRefs.java
          returns ZERO results for every pattern tried on this binary,
          including ".+" -- confirmed non-functional/string-poor binary, not
          a BLE-specific negative) and via the ISR-slot doc (single generic
          ISR slot, no per-source vector, nothing BLE-identifiable) but could
          not trace callers of the Meta-event senders because FindXrefsTo.java
          is confirmed still stale (hardcoded to old 0x801212e4 probe, known
          save_ghidra_script overwrite bug, not re-fixed). This is a real,
          flagged tool blocker for Part 3/4 of the new doc, not a guess -- see
          doc's Tool Note. Net: BLE link-layer EVENT REPORTING is confirmed
          ROM-resident and substantial; whether the lower-level RF/timing
          STATE MACHINE itself is ROM, patch, or hardware-sequenced remains
          genuinely open (would need a working xrefs-to tool or a fresh batch
          script to resolve -- both wairz script pools were reported full in
          earlier sessions, not re-verified this pass since no new script was
          attempted).

[DONE]  Document the encryption engine (E0 / SAFER+ / AES-CCM) (2026-06-21)
          BT classic and BLE security procedures' cipher implementation.
          Currently zero coverage — only the SSP IO-cap *trigger* path
          (FUN_80025b68) is documented, not the cipher itself.

          Found and fully decompiled the SAFER+ block cipher: core round
          function (0x8002cddc), key schedule (0x8002cb2c), bias constant
          (0x8002ca88), and exp/log S-box table pointers (0x8002cf1c/20 —
          symbol names literally say PTR_CRYPT_SAFER_*). Traced 3
          Bluetooth-spec-shaped wrappers down to the cipher: FUN_8002d00c
          matches E1 (2-pass SAFER+ -> 4B ACO + 12B SRES) and FUN_8002d14c
          matches E21/E22 (16B key + 16B block -> 16B output). Confirmed the
          LMP_* encryption procedure handlers (LMP_COMB_KEY_0x09,
          LMP_AU_RAND_0x0B, LMP_SRES_0x0C, LMP_ENCRYPTION_MODE_REQ_0x0F,
          LMP_PAUSE_ENCRYPTION_AES_REQ_0x66) are pure protocol state
          machines with NO cipher math inline -- they all call down through
          a small set of shared wrappers into the SAFER+ core above.

          E0 stream cipher and AES-CCM were searched for (LMP encryption
          handler cluster, BLE Meta-event cluster, AES-named LMP procedure)
          but NOT located in ROM software -- no LFSR-shaped loop, AES S-box,
          or MixColumns pattern found anywhere. Most likely both are
          hardware-offloaded via the same hook architecture already
          documented in rom/reverse_engineering_hardware_layer.md
          (bos_base+0xe4 / FUN_8004f824) -- plausible but not confirmed;
          flagged as open follow-up, not a tool blocker.

          Doc: analysis/rom/reverse_engineering_encryption_engine.md (new).
          Added to analysis/INDEX.md per its keep-current rule.

[DONE]  Document USB/UART transport framing and the ROM-side HCI driver (2026-06-21)
          How raw USB/UART bytes become HCI packets before reaching the VSC
          dispatcher already documented in reverse_engineering_vsc_dispatcher.md.

          Traced backward from assoc_w_tHCI_CMD (0x80020ee0). The direct
          caller was NOT found -- confirmed (not assumed) both xref tools are
          unusable for this: FindXrefsTo.java still runs stale content
          (prints the old 0x801212e4 target), and DiagAddr.java's
          "Symbols@target" xref section returns empty even for a function
          with a KNOWN, disassembly-confirmed direct caller
          (HCI_CMD_OGF_01__Link_Control, called via jal from inside
          assoc_w_tHCI_CMD itself) -- proving the tool exposes no xref data
          at all, not "zero callers." No new script could be written to do a
          jal-byte-pattern sweep (both script pools still full per prior
          tickets).

          Despite that, found real, previously-undocumented material:
          working backward from called_at_end_of_every_HCI_CMD_via_fptr
          (0x80009f68) turned up a cluster of 4 ring-buffer drain functions
          at ROM 0x80009da8-0x8000a474 (Kovah's own GZF labels
          early_fptr1/5/6/7, never indexed in kovah_function_list.md), each
          draining a circular queue (8/16/16/32 slots) of completed
          transfers. One of them (FUN_8000a1c0) explicitly builds an HCI
          Event packet and calls a sink with literal arg 4 -- the HCI H4
          transport type-byte for Event (1=Cmd/2=ACL/3=SCO/4=Event) --
          direct evidence of a transport-to-HCI bridge. A sibling function
          (FUN_8000a310) is a 3-channel enable/disable/reset state machine
          (interrupt-disable-protected register writes via the already-
          documented disable_interrupts/enable_interrupts jalx pair),
          matching a USB endpoint model (e.g. control + 2 bulk/int pipes)
          far better than a single UART line -- consistent with UB500 being
          USB-only. Found a RAM control-block region (~0x80120200-
          0x80122564) distinct from bos_base/config_base, i.e. USB transport
          has its own hook/control-block family separate from the
          BT-protocol-level one. Inbound ACL/SCO paths and the literal
          4-way packet-type-byte branch were searched for but not found --
          left as open work.

          Doc: analysis/rom/reverse_engineering_usb_transport_hci_driver.md
          (new). Added to analysis/INDEX.md per its keep-current rule.

PHASE 9 CONTINUED — EXHAUSTIVE RE OF EVERY ROM FUNCTION (full coverage, not just themes)
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Phase 9's initial backlog (above) was a thematic walkthrough — boot/reset,
interrupts, HCI router, LC/LMP, BLE, encryption, USB transport, a 33-fn
consolidation batch, and a function index — and it's done. But per
analysis/rom/rom_function_index.md, that walkthrough only brought 57 of 2739
ROM functions (2.1%) to "high confidence" (decompiled + written up). The
other 2682 are either completely unnamed (2278 FUN_8000xxxx, never triaged)
or named-but-thin (404: 105 medium-confidence one-liners + 299 low-confidence
Kovah names with unclear purpose, neither decompiled).

Goal now: drive every one of those 2682 to "high confidence" — full decompile
+ purpose + (where confidently established) a real Ghidra name — or, for the
genuine non-functions Ghidra's auto-analyzer mis-split out (1-byte alignment
stubs, switch-table case labels, thunks), an explicit one-line note saying so
instead of silently leaving them unlisted. Sweep by address region using the
8 buckets already computed in rom_function_index.md (each region's count
below = its own unnamed total + its own thin-named total, both computed
2026-06-22 from that doc):

  0x80000000-0x8000ffff: 307 unnamed + 27 thin-named (16 med/11 low) = 334
  0x80010000-0x8001ffff: 268 unnamed + 130 thin-named (64 med/66 low) = 398
  0x80020000-0x8002ffff: 321 unnamed + 63 thin-named (19 med/44 low) = 384
  0x80030000-0x8003ffff: 290 unnamed + 17 thin-named (0 med/17 low) = 307
  0x80040000-0x8004ffff: 307 unnamed + 12 thin-named (2 med/10 low) = 319
  0x80050000-0x8005ffff: 354 unnamed + 10 thin-named (2 med/8 low) = 364
  0x80060000-0x8006ffff: 238 unnamed + 94 thin-named (1 med/93 low) = 332
  0x80070000-0x8007ffff: 193 unnamed + 51 thin-named (1 med/50 low) = 244
  TOTAL: 2278 unnamed + 404 thin-named = 2682 functions to resolve

This is a LARGE undertaking — no single worker turn will finish a whole
64 KiB region (precedent: the Phase 1-8 consolidation ticket fully resolved
33 pre-characterized functions in one turn; these are colder, less
pre-characterized, so expect a similar or smaller per-turn throughput).
**Mandatory splitting rule for these region tickets** (overrides the generic
wip-loop "mark DONE or BLOCKED, never leave [NEXT] open" rule's *finality*
implication — it still applies, just via self-chaining instead of true
completion):
  - Triage as many functions as you can with real decompile + evidenced
    purpose (not guesses) this turn. Use mcp__wairz__run_ghidra_headless GZF
    process mode with existing generic scripts (DiagAddr.java/
    DecompileAddr.java with 0x-prefixed script_args — confirmed working

NOTES
-----
- All addresses are runtime (patch at 0x80100000, ROM at 0x80000000)
- The GZF is the authoritative analysis source (has ROM + runtime patch image)
- Raw rtl8761bu_fw.bin (42088 bytes) = patch only; no ROM; limited for analysis
- config_base and bos_base are runtime pointers; their values (~0x80121200) come
  from the ROM's BT state allocation, not from the patch itself
- wairz GZF process mode: use_saved_project=True gives access to all three blocks
  (patch at 0x00000000, rom at 0x80000000, data at 0x80100000). script_file_id
  and script_name both work in this mode (path bug fixed 2026-06-08).
- Firmware format: magic(9) + fw_version(4) + unknown(3) + num_patches(2) +
  IC_subver[n](2n) + patch_offset[n](4n). 2 patches at 0x30 and 0x3780.
- Address mapping in GZF process mode: patch block uses FILE offsets (0x00000000+);
  ROM block uses runtime 0x80000000+; data block uses runtime 0x80100000+.
- Address mapping in raw import mode (old): runtime = Ghidra_addr + 0x00100000.
- Master installer literal pool: Ghidra 0x800039F4–0x80003BC0 (patch block = file addr)
- Patch entry called by ROM: runtime 0x8010A001 (Ghidra 0x8000A001)
  → Ghidra can't decode this region (MIPS16e EXTEND pcode errors)
- String-assoc installer: FUN_8010e27c (52B) installs 6 protocol dispatch handlers
  into dispatch struct at 0x8012ae8c. Called by ROM 0x80009990 hook mechanism.
  See analysis/reverse_engineering_protocol_dispatch_layer.md.
- Address-pair table at file 0xA0 (runtime 0x801000A0): OMIT for libre (2026-06-10).
  No consumer in ROM/patch; DATA block zeros; outside single-patch FC20 window.
  → analysis/reverse_engineering_address_pair_table_omit.md
- MIPS16e handler stubs region was a MISIDENTIFICATION: 0x8010A160-0x8010A2FF is
  the CODE BODY of FUN_8010a000 (patch entry). GZF PROCESS MODE decodes correctly.
- Vanilla vs GZF: rtl8761bu_fw.bin = 42088 bytes; GZF patch block = 44484 bytes.
  Extra 2396 bytes at 0x8010A468-0x8010ADC3 = Kovah's "dark firmware" (analysis
  code). GZF also contains 'rom' block (ROM dump via VSC FC61) and 'data' block
  (runtime RAM snapshot with sub-installers). Both blocks are encoded in the GZF
  ZIP but inaccessible via wairz run_ghidra_headless (always loads vanilla binary).
  GZF accessibility: ROM and DATA are in the GZF file; wairz's import always
  resolves to the raw binary. Ghidra GUI can open GZF directly for full access.
- Hardware regs: MMIO at kseg1 0xb000xxxx (physical 0x1000xxxx). Register r/w
  via ROM fns at runtime 0x8001136c (read) and 0x8001139c (write).
